Tool calls:  [ToolUseBlock(id='toolu_01E27kHGTBbLLQXZEnCucgFr', input={'coworker_name': 'Emily', 'message': "Here's a beginner-friendly guide to quantum computing:\n\n1. Quantum Bits (Qubits) and Superposition\nThink of a classical bit as a coin lying flat - it's either heads (0) or tails (1). A qubit is like a spinning coin - it exists in both states simultaneously (superposition) until observed. \nExample: A password cracker with classical bits tries each combination sequentially, while quantum bits can try all combinations simultaneously.\n\n2. Quantum Gates and Circuits\nClassical computers use AND, OR, NOT gates. Quantum computers use special gates like:\n- Hadamard gate (H): Creates superposition\n- CNOT gate: Entangles qubits\nAnalogy: Classical gates are like light switches (on/off), quantum gates are like dimmer switches (infinite positions).\n\n3. Quantum Entanglement and Teleportation\nEntanglement: Two qubits linked so measuring one instantly affects the other, regardless of distance.\nAnalogy: Think of twin dancers - when one moves, the other instantly mirrors them, no matter how far apart.\nTeleportation: Not Star Trek! It's transferring quantum states between particles using entanglement.\n\n4. Quantum Algorithms\n- Shor's Algorithm: Efficiently factors large numbers (threatens current encryption)\nExample: Classical computer factoring 300-digit number = millions of years\nQuantum computer = minutes\n\n- Grover's Algorithm: Searches unsorted databases quadratically faster\nExample: Finding a name in an unsorted phone book - classical computers check each entry, quantum computers find it much faster\n\n5. Healthcare Applications\n- Drug Discovery: Simulating molecular interactions\n- Protein Folding: Understanding disease mechanisms\n- Personalized Medicine: Analyzing genetic data\nExample: Testing millions of drug combinations simultaneously instead of sequentially\n\n6. Current Limitations\n- Decoherence: Qubits lose information quickly\nAnalogy: Like trying to keep many coins spinning perfectly\n- Error Correction: Quantum states are fragile\n- Scalability: Currently limited to few hundred qubits\n- Cost: Requires extreme cooling (-273°C)\n\nKey Points to Remember:\n1. Superposition = multiple states simultaneously\n2. Measurement changes quantum state\n3. Entanglement enables quantum advantage\n4. Not always faster than classical computers\n5. Best for specific problems (factoring, search, simulation)\n\nBegin with these basics and gradually explore more complex concepts. For hands-on experience, try IBM's Quantum Experience platform - it's free and lets you create simple quantum circuits.\n\nLet me know if you need clarification on any of these concepts!"}, name='help_coworker', type='tool_use')]

Transformer Architecture\n\na) Self-Attention Mechanism:\n```python\nclass SelfAttention(nn.Module):\n    def __init__(self, d_model):\n        super().__init__()\n        self.q = nn.Linear(d_model, d_model)\n        self.k = nn.Linear(d_model, d_model)\n        self.v = nn.Linear(d_model, d_model)\n        self.scale = math.sqrt(d_model)\n    \n    def forward(self, x):\n        Q = self.q(x)  # Query\n        K = self.k(x)  # Key\n        V = self.v(x)  # Value\n        \n        # Attention weights\n        scores = torch.matmul(Q, K.transpose(-2, -1)) / self.scale\n        attention = F.softmax(scores, dim=-1)\n        \n        # Output\n        return torch.matmul(attention, V)\n```\n\nb) Multi-Head Attention:\n```python\nclass MultiHeadAttention(nn.Module):\n    def __init__(self, d_model, num_heads):\n        super().__init__()\n        self.num_heads = num_heads\n        self.attention = SelfAttention(d_model // num_heads)\n        self.proj = nn.Linear(d_model, d_model)\n    \n    def forward(self, x):\n        # Split into heads\n        batch_size, seq_len, d_model = x.size()\n        x = x.view(batch_size, seq_len, self.num_heads, -1)\n        x = x.transpose(1, 2)\n        \n        # Apply attention\n        x = self.attention(x)\n        \n        # Combine heads\n        x = x.transpose(1, 2)\n        x = x.contiguous().view(batch_size, seq_len, d_model)\n        return self.proj(x)\n```\n\n2.
